O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	Here is the translation of the text line by line:
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I would complete this treatise for you, which is part of the work of the hands, that is to say, "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of the hands is done in our region and is strange to all, it is very difficult to comprehend its science and scope, and there is nothing left for the force that moves the hands but to describe in books the small movements of the ancient hands.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this origin comes error and vanity, and intentions are closed and science is alienated.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	Or me seems that I will make it new life along the order of this doctor according to the way of exposure and proclamation and abbreviation; and shall come along the forms of the iron instruments of cauterization, and other tools of the work with the assistance of the proclamation and preparation of him, as is fitting.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for the reason that no good masters of hands are found in our land, the art of medicine is prolonged.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for him who deals with it to rise in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so much that he knows the judgment of the members, and their forms and connections and separations of vessels, and has knowledge of the bones and nerves and blood vessels and the number of organs, and the movement and rest of veins, and the place of their issue.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And for this reason, as Iopas says, no one is good with the hand alone, and with the work it is little; and most of all in the art of hands.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We say to you in the introduction of this book that whoever is ignorant of the things said above should be careful not to make mistakes and harm people; so that I have often seen many of those who meddle in this science and abandon themselves to ignorance and unproven theories.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a foolish man who cut an abscess of scrofula or the neck of a woman, and he cut the arteries at the base of the neck; so that there was so much blood that the woman died in his hands.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And I saw another foolish man who took a stone from a man's bladder, and the stone was large; so he took a piece of the bladder with him, and he died in three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have already seen it called for by the law, and I saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone; and if he were to remove it, he would surely die.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And see this other man who came to cure.i. duke of our land who had his leg broken, and with the break he got a wound; and the doctor ignorant pulls out the break on top of the wound by strong medicine, and leaves nothing in the wound but pain, and so he left it; and he ordered that he not take it off; and he waited until the leg was all healed and his foot and came to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and I hurried to dislocate the leg; and when I had dislocated it, he was at peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But every way of corruption was confirmed in him or the member, and he could not heal it; and the corruption did not cease to spread through the member until all the members were lost.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And see this other man who came to cure.i. an abscess that had become putrid, and then inflamed because of the wickedness of his lordship.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For chancre, when it is purified of melancholy humor, it cannot but be touched with iron if it is not in its proper place so that one can completely destroy what is corrupt.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And for this reason, you skilled artisan, you need to know that the work of hands is divided into .ij. divisions: namely, where there is danger in many dispositions; and I will show in each of these in this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	For by doing so, you need to keep yourself safe, so that the foolish person cannot speak ill of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	If you take your weapons with caution, and undertake your tasks lightly but firmly, and use the better path so that by the grace of God you come to salvation and are loosed; and reject those weapons that make you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you can come from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.»	Gallein says in some of his admonitions: "Do not take on the care of bad diseases, lest you be called a fool."
J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc .iij. chapitres.	I have devised this treatise according to .iij. chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapters are about fire cautery and medicinal water, and the chapters ordered from the beginning until the end; and forms of instruments, and tools for cauterization, and all that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapters are about cutting and piercing, and sucking up blood, and extracting arrows, and similar things; and the chapters are ordered and the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter deals with restoring dislocations and torsions, and similar things; and it is ordered that the bones be cut at the joints, and the forms of the instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Thus we remember the work; it is necessary that I speak of the quality of aid and the harm of each color.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of aid and harm is the longest word and the most subtle science, and its responses are hidden; and many wise men would speak of it, and agree with what I say; and I am short of words, for I shorten them.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that fire is universal aid to all colors, except for the two colors; that is to say, color hot in substance and color dry in substance.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In hot and dry combination of substances, some agreed and said that fire cautery is great aid; and the other said the opposite: that cautery does not help in diseases that come from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the fire's nature is so hot, and should not be cured with heat but by cooling it down; and he who says the opposite that fire cautery does great aid to hot and dry diseases that come upon men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of man and his moisture with the fire's complexion, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have never found this by experiment.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And any path, don't get involved in it but those who have experimented and know through long use the ointment of cauterization, and the diversity of complexions of men, and their dispositions and causes of their illnesses, and remedies and space of ten; we do not fear other complexions, however, for cold and moist illnesses.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all this will come together and agree with the cauterization.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, children, that fire cauterization is effective for the cure of secretions, and is of greater benefit than fiery medicinal cauterization.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and comes not forth but to the limb which is cooked, and harms no other member so much.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	Burning remedies come from one limb to another by removing, and cause disease in the limb for cure; and perhaps the sickness will be brought back.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Fire, due to its greatness and goodness of its substance, does not cause this, if there is no excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And I have found this by experience and by the length of service and study that I have put into the art, and is based on the truth of things; and because I do not like to steal the secret of fire, which is hidden in fire, and the quality of the work, how it cures diseases of the body, as the philosopher says in his proof; so receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they should be made at what time the cauterizations should be done, and they should be prayed over.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cauterization is suitable in all seasons, for because the imminent harm is overcome by the aid of the cauterization; and most especially the cauterization is for necessary pains without delay so that they cannot wait for the time when greater harm may come to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And I do not think at all, son, as they do; for because the disease that is cured by cauterization has no return; and it serves thus: but it is not so as they think, since cauterization is only medicine that changes the complexion, and dries up the humors that are the cause of pain, and worth more than medicine for the swiftness of its effect, and for its excellence and nobility.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And it is possible that the disease will come again according to the complexion of the patient and the place of the disease and its virtue; and are assembled in it the excesses by the acquisition of meat and similar things, if it is not administered cauterization at the place where there is little excess and moisture, as is administered for the pain, and the similar things, and the pain does not return again; but that happens little.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why the remedies are called medicinal remedies, and that is so; but they do not believe that the remedies are worth anything after medicine, but their understanding is wrong, and the remedies are the medical remedies because when we administer them in any disease, they do not work, then we administer the remedy, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Then open well that the remedies are the medical remedies, but not according to the understanding of foolish men.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that fire-poled remedies are more healing than those of iron, and they said that the quality of gold and its greatness of substance were the reasons; and they said that the heat of the remedy does not cause fever, but this is not true because I have experienced it, and I have found that in some people it does; and fire-poled gold remedies are more healing than iron, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And moreover, when you heat gold-poled instruments, you do not know when they are too hot by the color of gold, and they cool down very quickly; and if they are heated too much, they go out into the fire; and therefore there is enough impediment.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this we use fire cautery, which we have prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or you should read this chapter up to the point where the vision becomes clearer so that you may more easily find the way.
dou cautere olivaire	And the olive oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	For the olive oil cautery, apply it to the head, and in doing so, it will help with a variety of issues, including a disease called "soda," and due to multiple humors that affect the hair, ears, and cause many dreams and pain in the teeth and throat, and also many diseases caused by coldness.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the sick person be purged by a solution medicine, speaking the three days or according to what the virtue and the eagerness and the habit of the sick person can bear; and then do again the head of the sick person.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then make it sit crosswise between your hands, and place his hands on the sides of his neck; after that put the root of your palm on the root of his neck between his two eyes; and let come thy two knives, if he bleeds from then on heat the cautery which is called “olivare”, for this is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it over the ink mark, and as you descend and extract your hand little by little in turning it, then let your hand rest, and reward the place with a small hammer; and if you don't see the bone, then restart the cautery until you see the bone, as I told you; after that take 1.1 pound of silk, and put it wet and soft cotton inside, and put it over the mark, and leave it 1.3 days; after that put cotton soaked in oil on top; and let it be heated until the bone is cured; then cure the wound with the ointment which is called “tetrafarmaçon”, until it is well.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And say the ancient one, that however long the wound stays open, so much more it is purged; and for this reason if you help it.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And none of these said that one must let the cautery burn as much of the bone as is burned, and then resect what is burned from the bone, and be cured.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And another said that one must let the cautery burn as much as possible on the bone, and then cut off what is burned from the bone, and be cured; and one must let the wound remain open for a long time; after which one must cure and make it well.
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cauterizing do not seem to me to be good in all cases; they seem good only when there is a risk of death in a person; and I think that I should let it burn, for the shoulder joint is weakened by continuous solutions of nature, as we witness with other members; and even if the shoulder joint is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cauterization seems more gentle and milder to me, and from which I gather my experience, and thus I use it in all cases.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the old pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When in all the head comes a chronic pain, and lasts longly, then must use yeris and pills which are called "cochie", and head-washing and oils and plasters; and if one makes the fire cautery that we have above said, and it is not worth anything.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care if the patient's head is of a strong nature, and that he is not too cold; then cauterize him slightly as we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After you have made the fire cautery on each horn of the head as we have said above, and you have made the cauterization at the place which is called "vesselz"; and it is there where one sets the leeches; and align your hand so that you do not see the bone: the pain that the patient feels in this cauterization is much greater than in the others, and I will speak of it later; and it is necessary that the cauterizations of the horns be made finer than those at which one cauterizes the hair of the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	the fire cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When in one side of the head there is sudden pain, and it extends to the nape until the oil, and the jaw is purged with medicines mondifyants, and have been done all other cures that I said in the division of diseases, and all this does not profit: then make cauterization according to .ij. ways, that is to say, with medicine water and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	When the pain in one side of the head extends to the back of the neck until the oil, and the jaw has been purged with medicines that make it mondify, and all other cures have not helped: then make a medicine cauterization by taking a dough of aloes, and removing the skin and covering it with .iij. pieces, and then returning the aloes to the skin; and when it is re-covered let it rest for .xij. hours; and then release it and treat it again with a dough of garlic, and leave the wound open for .ij. days or .iij.; and then put cotton dipped in balm on it as long as it will absorb.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the oil treatment until it is healed; and if you see that fire treatments such as those I have written or any other fire treatment are necessary, then do so.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere. Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	The fire cauterization if it is according to this manner. Heat the fire of which this is the form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And is called "close" because the head is made in the form of a clove or there.i. little of a corbeau, and in the middle with a small appearance; and put it on the sore place, and take your hand and turn the fire slightly a bit, until the half of the flesh of the cure is burned; and lift your hand so that the artery does not burn, which is away, and runs an abundance of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par .iij. jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After it has been dried with cloth, and put on the place for .iij. days; then I dip cotton in oil, and then cure the place with ointment until it is healed; and if you want to cauterize this migraine with the cautery which is called "cultellare", at all points, and be careful not to cover the artery in this migraine which is not old.
de emigraine	of migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you cure migraine as we have said above in the divisions of diseases, and do not profit from it, and see that the cautery before spoken of at all points does not hurt, then it comes that you heat the cautery which is called  "cultellare" until it is white; and sign so on the sore place a line of half an inch long, and hold your hand once, and turn it so that you do not cover the artery and that you come not to the jaw; and guard against the mandible that mutts when one chews, and the loins are not relaxed that come from the artery when it is coped, or copement has great fear and more importantly at those who do not know and who are not students and tested; and leave the work in mid-path; but I will tell you how sanc is stung when the artery is copied, and I will show you to the place where it hits in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait .ij. coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that this cautery does not suffice to the disease, and the patient is suffering, cauterize him with fire on his head as well, and cure the wound until it has healed; and if you see, administer the cautery which we have said or the extract of the artery with the cautery which has .ij. knives; and this cautery is better than that and more useful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	the pain of the ears from cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	For when pain in the ear comes from cold, and one has applied the حلول [solutive] medicines and other remedies which we have said in the chapter on the division of pains, and the pain does not subside, then heat this cautery which is called "poins," which has this form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les .ij. se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait .x. poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After heating the whole ear, or the inside of each ear where the pain is located, and moving away from the root of the ear then, having marked the spot, make 6 points in each ear; then heal the area until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	of the mouth torture
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	who must be cured by fire is only for those that move with fluid, as we have said in the divisions of the diseases; and not to do any fire on the similitudes that come from the heat and the stench of fish.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de .iij. cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des .ij. levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you cure this torture of fluid movement that comes from the heat and stench of fish, and there is no other remedy, then you should make three fire cauterizations: one in the root of the ear, another a little further away at the temple, and the third between the two lips; put the fire in the healthy part, and let it burn half of the cauterization before removing it; and this is the form of the cauterization:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And is the resemblance of the scalpel that we have put forward, but it is a little more subtle and it is necessary that the scalpel be a little thicker; after cure the place as I have said before, until it is healthy.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai .iiij. cauteres: .ij. sus les .ij. cornes dou chief, et .i. emmi le chief, et .i. ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is old and you treat it thus as we have said, it does no good, and the patient has no fever, then make .iiij. cauterizations: .ij. on the .ij. horns of the head, and .i. cut off the head, and .i. where it is called "vasselz" as we have said before, and also cauterize the mouth of the stomach; and be cured thus as we have said before.
de litargie	of chalk
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	This is a medieval medical text and the translation is as follows:
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai .iij. cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere .i. doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai .i. cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, .ij. autres sus les .ij. cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If he is well in this way, it is good; and if he is not, he makes .iij. cauterizations by cutting off the hair from the scalp to the neck, and leaving space between each cauterization of .iij. two big ones; and heal thus as the others, and if he struggles, and the patient suffers, he makes .i. cauterization in the middle; and if it is needed, .iiij. others on the .iiij. horns, and heal him as long as he is well; and let the cauterizations which are called "olive", be made thus as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	of the cold
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et .i. derrier et .iij. sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai .iiij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	to the head from cold
de l’epilempsie	against epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	against epilepsy
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai .i. cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et .i. cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	Et s’il est un enfant qui ne peut pas supporter le feu, on lui fait gargarisme et mastication avec des viandes sèches; après quoi on met son chef au milieu, et on lui fait .i. cautère selon ce que nous avons dit ci-devant, et .i. cautère sur sa nuque, et sur chaque cornet ; et si le malade est hors de lui et souffrant, on lui fait des cautères comme je l'ai dit à celui qui a la paralysie et la mollesse du cou, sur la colonne vertébrale et sur le cou, et on leur fait des cautères d'olivier selon la manière que j'ai dite.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child, one should make a subtle cauterization according to this method:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When due to melancholy there are excesses or corrupt and thick moisture, then one should make a partial cauterization as we have said to the one who has paralysis:
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if due to melancholy there is a declining excess of melancholy, and the body of the sick person is moist, then one should give him to drink something so that his brain is purified, according to what it says in front in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai .i. torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com .i. cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After resecting the head of the disease; after making .i. a well-formed tortoiseshell, also as a circle, so that it is placed under the head; and the patient's seat is crossed and held fast on all sides; then present the liniment, and moisten with old butter; and heat the fire moderately, so that the two may be able to drink it without suffering; after emptying the circle through the top of the head, and letting it cool down; and do this to the disease every week once with other good treatment, until he is well.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere. Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	Or if you want to cauterize with fire, making many punctures all over the place. This way of cauterizing moistens the skull evenly; and then put cotton wet in butter and in grease of goat's milk on it.
de l’awe des eulz	of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When awoke comes first as eyes by the signs that I have said in the division, then begin and do drink to the disease purifying the head, and warding off all moisture, and making him sweat or bathe many times while fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as .ij. eulz ensamble, ou en .i. se li dessendemens est en .i.; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After he has commanded his head to retreat, and made a fire cautery on the top of the head, and made 2 cauteries on each side of the temples if it has fallen out of place and is together, or if one side has fallen out of place, make it long according to the width of the temple; and guard against the evacuation of blood, and if you see too much blood coming out, then stop him with a cloth so that he can't breathe.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les .ij. os derrier.	And I will teach you how to stop the blood flow in the extraction of arteries and in cutting, the fire cautery is made so that it is stopped; and never make a fire cautery or hurt them behind the 2 bones.
dou cors des larmes	of the eyes.
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: .i. cautere emmi le chief, et .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples, et .ij. cauteres ou haiterel desoz les .ij. os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout .i. petit cautere.	When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed and are on the veins, or deluge the arteries which are in the appearance of the head outside; and one can see that it is cold and watery excess, then he makes the fire cautery that I have said at the beginning of the awes descending to the eyelids: 1 fire cautery on the top of the head, and 2 fire cauteries on each side of the temples, and 2 fire cauteries where they hurt behind the ears; and if it is necessary more, then he makes all small cauterizes.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	to dry up tears within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide .iij. nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai .ij. cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les .ij. sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you have finished making medicine as we have described in the division, and it does not benefit, then do three times a day the wine of the ill; after that, place the head back into position, and make a cauterization with olive oil fire; and make three cauterizations with the cautery called 'clavis' on the two scars, a little bit in the hair; and beware of the artery so that you do not cover it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cauterization called 'clavis':
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare». de coi ci est li forme:	When the paper of the oil is softened by disease and moisture, then the cauterization with this cautery called 'olivaire'. For this is the form:
Et se tu vues si fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see so many fire cautery on the same wound as long as the hair is; and do not release your hand until the third part of the paper has burned up according to the way I said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	the hair that points to the oil
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	No time has passed that the hair of the oils is converted to the parched, and strikes the oil, and it does one cautery according to .ij. ways: that is to say by fire, or by burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow. Car en l’ovraige de cet chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they are born and grow long and even, then put the patient on your side; sign upon the paper of the hairs a figure which is also like the furrow of the heart, and is the beginning of the sign with which to pierce the hairs; then cotton wet with smoke and musk root made into oil, then heat the cautery by which this form is made:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi .iij. jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterize upon the figure that you have signed a little and little often, so that the scar be burned in place; and the sign of the health of the work is that you see the paper retire, and the hairs stand up at the tip of the oil; then lift your hand, and leave it so for .iij. days, then put cotton wet with smoke into wax as much as the heating be burned; after the cure of the dressing until he is healthy.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And after these come the hairs, and the paper is softened then begin the cautery again at the same place, as you have done first; and if the hairs are gone, then cauterize until the paper is raised to its natural place, and is even, and do not prick the hairs into the oil.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en .i. oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en .i., et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse .i. poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The medical hot cautery is that you command the patient to let the hairs grow long and even, then make of parchment the shape of the furrow of the heart; then take French soap and live fire, each one a ½., and grind them together well; and do it hastily, so that it doesn't cool down again, then pour on the shape that you have made like the furrow of the heart, and put upon the paper of the hairs; and if the patient is in oil only for 1 hour at most, then work also in water both as well; and put cotton wet with smoke into an aban of smoke; and the head of the shoulder be in your side and open mouth showing, and press 1.5 times and pour the smoke cotton upon the medicine; and if the patient feels tingling from the medicine, he shall feel burning too, for he feels burning also as from fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	If you have done this for a long time, keep the medicine to your mouth.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien. Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the mordication has passed, lift up your jaw, and if you see that the paper is raised as though it were lifted by a constraint of fire or by an incision; and if so, it is good. But if not, put the medicine back on the spot where the medicine has not worked, until your teeth are even, and your gums are in place; then put cotton wet with balm on it until the aching stops, after treating the sore which is called "dyafenis" and others, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.  Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if you are in a position to well guard your teeth by great care that the medicine does not touch the gums at all. And if the paper becomes soft after, and the hairs come out in oil, then begin again the medicine on the same spot which has become soft from the paper itself, just as you did before; after treating until it is healed; and this is the form of the fuel of mirth:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the hair of men is different in length and thinness, and according to what it is like for you; and do not answer the right way to anyone who studies this craft.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	about the treatment of fistulas by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have described in the division of diseases, and your treatment does not help, then it is necessary that you apply cauterization according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to place his head in your lap; and dip cotton wicks in oil of mustard or apple juice on oil; then heat the cautery, which should be sharp: and set it against the hair at the root; if you see, so point it from one side to the other, like a tent; but nevertheless, what is most important is that it be sharp for your treatment.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	Then press the fistula if it is open, and treat the porosity, and dry it; and if it is closed, then open it again, and treat the bowel; after that, put a very hot cautery on it, and hold your hand over the cautery with oil, so that your hands do not play tricks; and put the cautery in the oil, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien. Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse .iij. jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se .xl. jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If you come to cauterize up to the bone, that would be good. If not, begin cauterizing again, and if you need to, leave it .iiij. days; after i put cotton wet with oil on it, and cure the wound-healing dry as long as it is healthy, and when .xl. days have passed and it is still healthy, I put medicine of corrosive water until the bone is uncovered; and treat according to what comes in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent. Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure .i. camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	And I have a way of cauterizing fistulas that no one of the ancients has said. Understand fistula, and pierce the place; after put in the incision .i. small needle of silk so as to be the form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and I make it in the quantity of one .Z. of plaster; and hold your hand or camahan firmly, and do not move the patient at all, so that the plaster melts and does not run to its oil; and it is good that you put cotton wet with oil on the patient's fistula, and rub it gently: the plaster if applied to the place of the fistula, and he heals with a wonderful cure.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin. Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery we have described, it is good. If not, let him give a piercing to the nose, and bring the fistula to the root of the nose according to what comes in his own chapter.

de l’aposteme de la goule	from the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre. dou movement des dens	the movement of the teeth

de la dolor des dens	of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu. Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cauterization with butter: If it is so that you squeeze butter from a milk-vessel, and the tip is made of iron or gold; after taking cotton and wrapping it on the tip of a needle, and the wetting in butter, and placing it on the aching tooth carefully, and keeping it as long as it becomes cold; and doing this often until its virtue comes to the root of the tooth, and if you see that the wool and cotton wet with butter become cold, and place it on the aching tooth, and place it on 1 gold tip as hot as possible.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain. Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	The fire cautery all together if it is such that you squeeze a tooth from iron or steel, and make large so that the fire does not come to the mouth of the patient; then heat the cautery, for its shape will come later, and put it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery is cooled; do this often, because the pain will be increased the next day or the day after. And it happens that the patient fills his mouth with good butter in the haste of the cautery, and then he swallows it; and this is the shape of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make a cauterization on the main tooth that you want, and according to what you have power; and this is the shape of the tooth:

When a vessel is broken and there is an opening and moisture and corruption, if you make a small hole in the place where it has broken, and keep the hole open, and heat the fire cautery that seems sharp to you, and pour it into the hole according to the quantity that the hole has entered, and then start again with the fire cautery as long as the corrupt and moistened flesh is burned, once or twice or according to the quantity of the need; and guard against touching the nerves that are there, and do not make a cut except in the boney part, and think that it does not persist; after you have healed the place until it is healthy, and the matter has been removed for a long time, then know that the place has been completely healed; and if the matter has not been removed, know that the place is threefold, and the bone at the bottom is corrupt; and thus as one of these that we will tell you in its place.

de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any limb

Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And know that the more I make cauterizes, the more I make help, and the profit is greater; and know that the patient does not feel pain at cauterizing as healthy people do, because the whole body is already corrupted. And it is necessary that cauterizes are large and small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you will find in the shape of iron. de enfleure	of flor

And never do a cautery except by hand or foot or back, at the exit of the nerve that moves the limb, so if inflammation comes from there; and yet there is no harm in doing so as long as one knows the limbs and the exits of the nerves moving the body.

li cure dou feu par fer	The cure by fire with iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. This putrefaction cannot be cured with just herbal medicine; however, fire cauterization is of great help, and I have already described how to treat putrefaction with herbal medicine based on its stage. des porrelz qui vienent as piez	Pores that come from the feet

quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut off
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l'artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l'incision de l'aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d'estenchier.

dou chief plein d’aigue	the head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit. And after the incision, remove all moisture. Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.
