For if the blood is black, let it run until it is red; and if you see a lump, let it stand until it is thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And for those who are sick and need to extract blood, make the wound larger, and keep the flames wide open;
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and to those who are weak, do the opposite, and it is necessary to heal them little and often, and one must heal them by cutting across, not by piercing.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this method of healing is preserved from the decay of blood and the cutting of nerves, and it is better than the long healing or the broad healing.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And to those whose bodies require healing, it is necessary to give them moistened bread made from grape juice; if they are heated, if the blood is troubled. Give three times or four times.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if he is of a cold complexion, give him moistened bread soaked in musk syrup, or honey syrup infused with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if it goes to the head, after the exit of the wind of blood, it is necessary that it hums the brew of wine and sweet-smelling syrup.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and use the other things that we have said in the division or chapter of fainting, for the evacuation of a vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if it vomits up the food in the arms, and sometimes feels pain, if it is weakened by great pain, that it heals little by little, according to the quantity of its continued virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if it vomits up the food in the arms after the first fainting, and has a strong constitution, then heal for .vij hours after the first faint, or after nine hours.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who must be healed on another side, if it should be healed on the second day or third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	For he has blood fever within the body, which makes heat and brings on a fever; so that, if there is a large amount, it must be drawn off, and the wound widened as much as it can ooze.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	and then you shall treat all the conditions for healing, and put your hand on his pulse as it heals, so that death does not come from pain.
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	and if this happens often, when healing is neglected;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it does not fit when you see the arm disconnected, and make it come out with blood for the second time, and the hole is closed, that you press firmly on top;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	if it is twisted, let him extend his arm carefully, for that would be bad;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but let it be until it has healed the second time; or you point to the tip of the flame, until the blood that is frozen at the base of the arm comes out;
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and put a little of salt on it, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if a vein has burst, let it alone and do not constrict it, until the abscess is calm.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if there is a need to drain blood for a second time, let it be done in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein that runs along the arm is to be used for bloodletting if there is a need to drain blood, because it is more accessible than the vein at the base of the neck.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the way to perform the bloodletting is that the patient holds his hand in warm water until it turns red.
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	Then let there be a gentle movement, so that the vein appears well, then keep it safe now by going through, not too wide or too long;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and make the joint wide enough, and keep the joint well near the hand, and so cannot pull it out, then put the hand in warm water, and let the blood run in the water until you have enough;
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is cold, then do not dip the hand in warm water, for we put it in more when it is cold than when it is warm;
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the vein that has been saved is safer from all other veins, there is no artery or nerve;
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The salve for the right hand saves from all liver diseases; and this is the method:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Draw out the hand, and bathe it in hot water until the vein has disappeared, if possible;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and wrap it up tightly with bandages, and cut off all of its hair, if necessary;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	and do not cut too deeply, for the nerves are very sensitive and can easily be damaged;
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and then put the hand in hot water, it is frozen in the wound, and cannot be taken out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the wound as much as necessary, put oil and thread to bind it firmly together, and do this for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The surgery on the left hand should be performed first for the disease of the mouse, and do all the rest as I have told you about the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The surgery on the thumb should be performed first for all the diseases that are apart from the hand,
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	If as diseases of the mare, and retention of flowers, and disease of the reins, and cuisses and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the quality of his health is that the patient drinks some warm water, and rubs the vein until it stops.
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and on top of the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot go many reins;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	For in this chapter, or more widely, at the rear, or at the ankle, that is how you treat it.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you treat it on the foot, beware of the nerves which are exposed, and treat it as you would a wound, and let the flames be quenched.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the person cannot walk, put the foot into water, and let the vein bleed well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if you treat it for the first time, start the second time above a little hole, because the blood is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	do not doubt about the nerves, as we have said before, and thus do the same for the other foot evenly.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The legs of the sciatic vein are at the ankle, and its pain extends to the hip, when it is due to cold.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the quality of this pain is that the patient gets in or out of the bath, and pulls it off the ankle .iii. two with turning,
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	For otherwise the vein does not open; and if it opens, so that you can feel it in all ways, and by passing;
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it is worth more than you can cope, for the leg is out, and she is very well returned to many men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not treat it, unless there is a rain from him who opens or closes the foot, and towards the little toe, and keep away from the nails;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	and make so much run of the blood that you see it, and then untie the ligature, and put on cotton and hold it fast; it is now healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	Wounds from suction cups
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	are made of horns, or of glass, or of stone; and the suction is made in one of two ways: either by hurting and drawing out blood, or without hurting.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this ventilation which is not to hurt, depends on 2 ways: or it is all fire, or without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and ventilation which is done by hurting and by extracting blood depends on 13 parts of the body,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	of which one is all in the chest; and the other is in the throat;
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and 2 others in 2 coasts of the throat; and 1 below the chin;
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the suction of the .i. shoulder blades; and the suction on the shoulders;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and the suction of the .i. arms; and the suction of the .i. legs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and the suction of the 11th leg; and the wind-suction does not treat blood, except for small veins that are scattered in the chest;
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and so that it does not afflict anyone, unless it is done like this, as it is done for a vein;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and does not need to be cooked, nor boiled, in any illness that comes from overeating, until all the body is empty.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if, because of necessity or custom, we cook it every hour at the beginning of the month or at the end, and in each month;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are those who, when they need to vent their food, do so gradually;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and if there are those who, after ventosing, have inflammation and pain in their face, and in their neck, and darkness in their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and those who vent a drop of blood into their mouth, and have fled the tongue, and seek blood.
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and if any of these people are sick, and see no blood nor vomit nor death nor similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is the third month of the year, we order that they be ventosed after.iij. hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The surgeon of the museum should assist in the treatment of the disease of the head ... if there is pain and it does not come until after the whole body has been evacuated.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	and this ventilation if it is in place of the health of the cerebral,
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and it does not suit that person who is of a cold complexion to drink, or who has had a fever, because this does them great harm;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and for this reason it does not suit that person who is of a cold complexion to drink, or who has had a cold;
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And whoever drinks this often becomes confused, and for this reason the fire cautery should be placed a little further back due to the confusion that results from drinking it.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The ventilation of the neck is located in the place of the windpipe at the base of the skull and for this reason it is subjected to stretching of the larynx.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and at the slit of the channel of the throat, and all around, and at filling up;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it is necessary to push it back, because if it holds too firmly, then in the jaw or stomach or somewhere else.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The ventilation of the neck is located in the place of the windpipe at the base of the skull and for this reason it is subjected to stretching of the larynx.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and is in the area of the saint's shrine; and it is necessary that you instruct the doctor that he express his hand to the patient, that he does not cut the artery, and does not cause bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The vents of the mouth bring about a disease of the mouth and a corruption of the gums and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and is in the area of the saints' lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The vents of the shoulders bring about a disease that comes from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The vents of the arms, up to three veins, bring about a disease.
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	For she brings pain from these great veins.
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instruct the surgeon that he does not cut too deeply, for the bones are naked and there are many nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The suction cup that is on the back so it is attached to the fundament, and to the glands, must be large, and of metal, for it has a task of good milking; and by chance, if it were too small, it would break; and it would make great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The suction cups of the legs so open, for they attract blood from all the body, and cause old pains of the kidneys, and of the uterus, and of the bladder, and bring forth fluids; and they are in place of the iij. sophenes, and the iij. chevilles, and altogether they weaken the body after long use, and bring about premature death in many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	Here is the translation of the text line-by-line into English:
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	"And if the skin is thick, so it is necessary to hurt .ij. times: the first time to soften the path of the large skin sore."
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	"And if the skin is very thick, so it is necessary to hurt the third time; and when we want to squeeze the small sore little by little, we must hurt once only."
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	"And if we want to suck blood, so we begin often; and if the skin is thick, so we should be firm, and the end should be that the piercing be heard suddenly,"
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and cover with oil the places of the suckers, which are large and hard, so that they become soft;
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is swollen, with oil of violets, or oil of sweet almonds, or oil of cucumber seed;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is hot, with oil of water-cress, or of lily, or of chamomile, or other kind.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is thick and cold, take oil of amaranth, or of balsam, or oil of fennel, and other kinds.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if someone has a sore that is tender and large, then one should not put any oil on it.
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	but it is necessary to wash after the windification with rose water, or cold water, or water of mulberry, or water of cucumber, or water of porcelain, or other similar things.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And if one has moisture, if it comes from there, or from water of Myrrh, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And if one has great excesses, they come from old wine, or water of fennel, or a decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar things;
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and do not fit to be pulled by suction before the bath nor bathe, but after a bath an hour or two; and do not sleep after suction.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and it is necessary that he warm up when he should be suctioned and when he has been suctioned.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And beware if the person being treated is colicky, and if the poultice is too hot or burning.
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	if it is necessary that he consume cold things, such as pomegranates, endive, and lettuce, and milk, and similar foods;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and minced meat, and cheese of the goat, and wet meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	and those with a pale complexion, if they drink syrup of honey and fragrant wine that is between old and new, and minced meat, and minced poultry and small birds and pigeons;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and on the day that they feel wind, if they drink more than they eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is convenient to give to some men triple or musk before the wind, or after, in order to strengthen the main members;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and make it thin, but it only works for those who are hot from drinking.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The leeches that are used to sting are those that are put on the liver, and the mouse, and the podagra, and on the belly and the bowel and the rain and the hernia, because this member does not bear stinging on the skin,
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and they are not done so much as to draw blood from one member to another,
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	as we do with the mammary glands when the milk comes out; by removing the viscosity that is in the member, as we put leeches on the belly and on the bowel to reduce the member.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and bone the pain, when there is an operation or stone, if by its own virtue bone attracts the operation, or deserts the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	and thus do so when you put it on the liver and on the midsome when there is repressed wind.
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	and these suction cups are empty only to suck up so little; and never are they together, fire, and never are there plainness of water.
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	as such diseases of the pleurisy, and in such a way that the suction cup is filled with hot water, or with water in which it has boiled herbs suitable for this purpose.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the suction cup administered to fire is thus:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And it should be 2.5 inches wide and a half palm long, and it should have or is at the center a small hole, as for inserting an needle
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and let it be of iron, so that it does not damage the patient when applied to the member;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	and has in the center a crossbar of iron or of metal, for the purpose of taking a candle grip;
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and be long and short according to the diseases and the age of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	For the suction cups of children are other than those of old people, and thin ones that fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And it is necessary to place this suction cup on the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	take the candlewax or .i. ointment, and put it in the middle of the suction cup at the root of the penis, which is placed on the middle of the suction cup,
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the clarity is at the bottom of the suction cup so it does not burn the patient.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it on the member, and these two are at the top of the hole that we have said, so that when you turn it over, if there is steam, and heat the suction cup;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and take the lining as before, and renew it often, if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the suction cup is now ready for the disease of pleurisy, in all water, has no verge or hole, and is prepared only when it is plain water, and placed on the member with such a little movement.
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	are not brought together except in members or one cannot put the suction cups because of their smallness, as lips and gums, and similar them;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in the naked legs of a horse, as two or three or others;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of use so that when you find suction cups that are in clear water without danger, if you take them.
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put them in water for as long as they are familiar, and do not have anything in their bellies;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then clean from the vein and the wound, then rub the limb until it is red, and put the poultices on;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are healed, and have cherried, if it is his or one that can be put a wound, it is put on because this works well after.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, raise the head in such a way, and then water, very well, and then rinse it out;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and let him lie too long after the heart of the sun, if moist. i. linen cloth in cold water, and put on, as long as the sun is wet;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the sun is multiplied, then put on vitriole ground, or gall, and similar things, as long as it is dried up;
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or put on the ground half of peeled peas, and leave them until they burn at the ground, now it will be dried up;
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you have more work, then take other veins.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the pus does not want to take, then rub the site of the wound with fresh blood, or put an needle in it as long as there is pus coming out.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	and then place them on, and soon as they feel the pain, so they burn;
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are crying, then powder on a little alum and honey, or oak bark powder, or ash powder, so they will not cry anymore.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This is the beginning of the book about fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	The chapter on cauterization is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is a remedy for fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, you wise person, that the wise man will pour this chapter on cauterization, which no ancient book or letter has ever mentioned.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	And for this reason the science is strange to our land, for I never found any good book about it.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing, except for the knowledge of the ancient books, which I have studied so much and treated about the science, and by experience, and by the custom of my life;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained therein, and I have shortened it at the end, and I have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, as I have done in these 20 chapters above.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore it is appropriate that we say in this book the sum of the words and the chapters where wisdom dwells, and delay upon truth, so that those who are tested may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when fracture or dislocation or torsion or dislocates comes to someone, it is appropriate that you hurry to save the sick person from one side and the other, if there is no pain on either side, as in weakness of the body, or infirmity, or age;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	or if the tendon is too tight or too loose; and mild drinks too often, that is to say, cold juices, and cheese and herbs, and do not drink wine, and do not eat any foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have no doubt about the appendix, nor about the expansion of matter in the member; if the disease returns to its first governance which it has used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that the patient be fed with food that makes fat, or has viscosity like cooked bread, and rice, and beans, and pies, and cakes of milk, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For a slow healing reduces the break and makes it heal faster.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that broken bones of old people and the feeble cannot recover or strengthen themselves according to their nature because of the lack of blood in the limbs, nor those that are too soft, like the bones of small children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	but has no cure, return to the broken bone. large bones that join together the member, as much as it heals, and for this reason there is no need to feed it with large meat, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that the breakers are various in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break of the head is other than the break of the leg or foot, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of breaks.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a break that goes to the root, and another in the joint, as when one cuts the hair with scissors.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a break with a wound, and a break that is just a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And at every mode there is his own instrument, and his own tool for restoration, according to that which the memory comes in its place.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and is caused by the fracture of the bone by that which the lever is twisted and opened well on one side, and is pressed with the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no torus or twist in it, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no fracture;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can have torus, or crack, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is not necessary for you to move it with your hand, but put on the medicine that comes next, and then hold it now gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the break that goes in the arvolt, and are the three parts separated, it now seems to put them together evenly, so that the abscesses come out.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if the abscesses come out, so you leave no time, as long as the abscesses are calm;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Then put it evenly on the medicine that you can easily and thoroughly apply, and know that the restoration of it is lighter than the restoration of that which has pieces; then hold it, as it seems hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if in the bone there are pieces broken, and they are of .ij. parts, be it hand or foot, or at your hand if it is a small member, or at .ij. strings, or at a string and at your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and set the member according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken member are healed, you will bring back all additions in their places by means of which you can, and keep so that your work does not cause the patient any injury or pain;
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and set well the 2 joints of the bone according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel well with the hand if it seems to you that it is not well: if it is well put together, and do not strain it too much, do not press it as they do by their work of incising aching and contracting the member, as we have often wanted many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limbs are at rest, teach the patient that he not move them, neither while awake nor asleep, nor while turning over, nor in any other way.
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and guard well that the limbs be so secure that they feel no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when one feels no pain, then it is at rest, and one should put it in a position where it feels no pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and guard well that it be placed correctly, so that there is no twitching when it is reset.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the broken member is according to what I told you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	You should know that broken members are various in size and length and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are small limbs, such as breasts and toes and similar things: it is convenient to wrap sheets of soft linen around them;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	and those that are thick, such as thigh and leg: it is convenient to wrap with a wide and sturdy linen, for the wide linen embraces all of the large member, and holds it evenly together, so that there is no gap;
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	Then he should make light blows with his fist, 2 or 3 times according to the limb, and hold back the hand a little from the joint, then go above the break and hold it back less, so that the break then moves a little way away.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the joint a little and a little, until you press strongly on the sound side, then take another limb, and turn again above the broken place;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then go back to the sound side of the break and hold it gently, not too hard or too lightly, as we said in the first step about;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then put between the light threads of linen or drapes, until they are all even, then lay it all on top .i. bandage, and then put your well-made splints on, if there is an abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is an abscess or abscess, then put on something to calm the abscess and keep it open, and let it remain so for some days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then extract from your bones, and let them be half a foot long, or a broad cane, or a palm branch, and be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	But it is necessary that the bone that one puts on the fracture should be a little thicker and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and be also long or short according to the size of the member;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	Then bind them to the staves also as you did with the first hour, then lie upon one above a thread in the same way as on the first hour over the splint.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	then bind them more tightly, less so; and it is necessary that the thread be medium, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of linen;
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the thread is thick, like the ropes of linen that they make into ligatures, and it is a great error, for the ligature cannot be equal if it is too thin, and it is necessary that there be less than two inches of space between each string.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is pricked by the joints of the staves after they have been stretched, then let them be padded with linen, or woolen cloth, so that they do not bruise.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the fracture, and the curative is broken, I will say the cure hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it does not fit to extract all the members of a broken person the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the members are great, it does not fit to put on a cast before 2-3 days or more according to the severity of the injury to the appendix sometimes soon after;
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and here is the method of the ancient plaster to restore fracture, dislocation and twist: and it is that you take flour that holds to the walls of the mill, and confound it with a lot of eggs, and put this confect, not too clear nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common method of the plaster restoring the fracture to several dispositions, especially for women and small children, because it is not too sharp or too frosty.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren Z abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. Z.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. Z.; alechil .viiij. Z.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another way to make a plaster that restores breaks, dislocations, and twists: take mugat and vismalve, ana 10 Z.; myrrh and aloe, ana 67 Z.; acacia 5 Z., grind well, and confect with water or egg yolk, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another way to make a plaster for joints and bones that have come loose from their places, and to soothe pain that comes suddenly, and to repair the broken bone: take fresh milk and thicken it slightly with boiled oil, and apply it to the affected area. This plaster does not restore properly, but is good at soothing pain in an abscess, and properly repairs broken bones.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way to make a plaster that restores broken bones: take dried fig leaves and dried wood avens leaves, grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another method of plastering for the restoration of bone fracture and for lessening the remaining abscess. Take root of wormwood, chamomile, violet flower, flour of timothy, each of these in part; grind them and confect with wine, and the members will be warmed by it, confected with coriander seed juice or water, and used.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another method of plastering that is stronger than the first, when an abscess has become chronic and requires the restoration of the limb. Take roots of wormwood, flax seed, borage, melilot, and yarrow; flowers of violet and chamomile, each in part; grind them and confect with salt water or plain water or wine, according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, Ypocras states that for the restoration of a broken limb, one should use only a plaster made of wax and oil, and nothing else; he says that it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galenus states that one should use dry things that are a little warm, such as myrrh and aloe, incense, and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	Another method of plastering that is useful for lesions and pain: take mugwort and horsetail, or feathers from birds, viscera, and a rope made even, and grind them up, and make a plaster and lay it on. And then take care not to let the patient feel any pain, nor does the bone move out of its place; otherwise, do not remove it by hand every day.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain or itching comes to the place, or there is no rest or swelling, do not wait, and remove the plaster now; and take a light cloth, and a sea sponge moistened, and dip it in water, and lift it up until the itching stops, and the pain is relieved;
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	then leave the member rest for an hour, then put another dry cloth, moistened with water or rose oil, and lay it on a nut, until you are sure of the heat;
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let the inflammation of the limb rest, and alleviate the pain of the bone, then continue the gentle application, and a little ointment, and do not pull it as strongly as before; and gently until it is cured.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that abscess, redness, pain, and swelling have occurred all over, and you need to use ointment and bandages, then start again, as you did in the first place with evenness.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if that does not come to the limb as we have said, and do not separate it more than three times or four times or five times; and do not leave it for more than ten days, according to what is seen, until the break comes closer to the shoulder bone.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	Then hold it more tightly than before, and make the meat thicker as I have said above; and if you see that it is drying up faster than necessary, know that there will be no growth; but let it rest a while, and then continue to bind it.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	arose lo onques d'aigue chaude teede, toves lo desliies, et c'est chescun tier jor, et esleich un poc la lieure;
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	arose lo onques d'aigue chaude teede, toves lo desliies, et c'est chescun tier jor, et esleich un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.
des diverses manieres de brisure	des diverses maneras de brisure
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	For he has fractures which are made by the striking of an sword, and the collar bone all the way to the shoulder which is broken in two, so as to make a sound like a whistle; and therefore this manner of breaking is called "whistling".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword breaks the bone from above when piercing, and this manner of breaking is called "absolute"; and the wound of these two great or small fractures is great.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a collision within, or a fracture or a collar of stone, or a fall on stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a piercing fracture, which comes close to the edge of the bone which is broken in two, or which is on the bone, and this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if to a wound which is healed in the bone as fine as an awl, and is a small split, and for this reason this break is called "capilaire".
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound is made by a stone or by falling or by some other thing, and brings in a piece of bone down, and the head of the bone is like what the blacksmith does when he works on the kettles; if it enters between the stones.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And if there is a small head of bone which becomes moist, as is the head of a child;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	and I will speak about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all kinds of injuries from traction on them, and the investigation in tents, and by the corrupt cart that is over it.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hair-like appearance is created by what happens when one exposes the bone and rubs it, thus creating a black fracture.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the cure for a fracture, be cautious of accidents due to illness, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting, loss of understanding, extension, palms, feverishness, and the eyes burning and reddening, and other similar symptoms in multiple conditions, it is doubtful that it can be cured.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a promising accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the cure.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the new birth comes to you first, and it is in winter, it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day of the month.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, you must remove the bone before the seventh day of the month, so that the decay of the bone does not occur, and the accident that we have mentioned comes.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the break in the bone occurs only to the part that covers the skull, you must split it in half: and it is that you squeeze the chief of the disease, and uncover the bone in all ways that you can, and on the shape of the wound more suavely than you can.
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and if the decay of blood occurs when the bone is uncovered, or an abscess breaks out, assist him with what you have, and it is that you fill the space with wet cloth soaked in oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	and let the wound rest as long as the abscess is calm, and are sure of the evacuation of blood; then begin to cut through the bone, and it is done according to .ij. ways of work: one way is that you chop with a narrow edge in front, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I make another cut wider than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is that you have a number of different cuts, some narrow and others wide, and they are pointed, and are made of iron; and work lightly, so as not to wound the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and tough, so that you pierce it from within, as well as you bring the talons with trowels, not completely through so that the point does not go out beyond the bone; and you must have more than, so that each comes in its place at the tip of the bone, so that you have trowels for all the test; and this is the form of the 3.ij. ways of talons:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	Here is the translation of the text:
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and treated the bone, if it seems to you that you should place on it the little hook which is kept back from the bone with everything .i. another instrument resembling an incision, but it is necessary that it be less thick and more delicate than the other incision;
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	and if it does not hold back any small bones or scales, if the bone is lightly held with some instruments; then heal the wound with the tints and oils that we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	and the other method of work which is that which Galen says, which is more dangerous; and hold it very firmly, and this is his word:
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, where the fracture opens widely, so that when you have uncovered this part, then you shall drive out the head of this lens-shaped chisel, from which comes this form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And do not cut from one side, and this part is wet on 2 sides, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then take a small mallet on the top, so that you hit the bone lightly all around, and give yourself well protection from the cloth that is driven out;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	if it is attached to the bone, then the bone will be lightly hit, because when the bone is well hurt, and there is no fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone break of the os ne perce jus' to the toile, and the os is cut so little only by above, and there are small pieces, then consider this asperity, and scrape off the scales with a sharp razor, of which you must have different quantities, to adjust in each place the most suitable, according to the work and the figure of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you are in front of many razors, and then of more subtle ones, do not stop doing this until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other haircuts and subtle shavings, it is necessary that you bring to bear according to its adaptation; and this is something that has not yet been answered to those who have put their study in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the wound is infected, then it is necessary that you strain .i. a piece of linen cloth, according to the quantity of the wound, and soak it in oil, and put it on the wound; and let it rest for three or four days.
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	then take another piece of linen cloth, doubled in two or three pieces, and soak it in wine and oil, and put it on the first cloth; and make this lighter than you can, so that you do not aggravate the wound, then remove it after it has soaked;
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and let it be so. i. e. for a day or two, until the abscesses are calmed, then untie them, and administer medicines in the form of roots of plants, and flour of times, and incense powder, and aristologous, and similar things; and from these things make powder, and put it on the wound, and administer to them medicines that harm the world without pain;
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	and guard that the wound is clean, that you do not leave it to fester, nor do you let it gather bowel, for when the bowel gathers on the cloth of the skull, if it is corroded and rotten, it brings great evil to the patient; because when one puts a poisonous medicine on it, it burns from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care therefore, that no bad accident should come to the patient, as we have said, if it is uncertain without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if sorrow does not come from the medicine that we have put on it, which has virtue, then you should squeeze a part of honey and 2 parts of rose oil and glues 1 drapelet, and put it on the medicine.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then the treatment in the manner of the treatments that it knows, until he is healthy.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that the 18 bones of the neck are never broken by itself, for they are cartilaginous, and they do not break unless they bend or twist, and then heal.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the 18 bones is broken, then you should knock your little finger or knuckle on the neck, and set the break evenly with your index finger, and out of place at the end, until the neck regains its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do it lightly, and beware that the patient does not feel pain through your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the neck, and cannot return to its place, know that you should put it equal to the top of a small ray.
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the break is in two parts, then do not restore it otherwise, and hurry to restore it on the first day, if you can.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If it is not, after the seventh or ninth day, when the apothecary's poultices are no longer needed, then bind at the top of the neck with strips of linen cloth, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Then bind the other end to the other side, if the break is there too; and let the strips be wide enough to fill the openings at the neck.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	And they said that one should not dry the tents with hay, and each day. I do not think this is good, but it is necessary that the tent be dried with sheep's wool, and powder from a mill; then leave the tent, until the bone is hard, and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And do not use goose feathers in place of tents, and if it is. I.e., sheep's wool, dry it in the sun, and stand it up, and blow on the patient with it; or make a veil as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess appears while you are operating, so that it oozes, or if you use cotton moistened with oil, or a little of astringent powder.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if an abscess does not ooze, put paste on it from the outside, made of semolina flour and incense powder, confited with sheep's wool, then put on light poultices, and do not bind the wound.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	and if the fracture of the neck is small, and it is broken into small pieces, then extract them with appropriate instruments for this, then cut the wound, and treat things that harm the car, and bind it together, as with plasters and ointments appropriate to this.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if there is no pain within the neck at all, then treat the swelling, and put on bandages of plaster, until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the split in the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is split, and there is no wound, and the fracture is only slight, and it is not broken in two, except that it may curve inside, so that it can be made lighter.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the fracture is on the right side, place your index finger in the mouth of the patient; and if it's on the left side, place your index finger from your right hand into the fracture, and gently push it back into place, and use your other hand to hold it there, and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is crooked, then it is necessary that you arrange extension on either side to make it even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if there is movement or a tear, then strain it with a golden, silver, or silk thread; then put the mandible that is broken over this, and put two sheets of cloth on top of it; and place a long, wide piece of leather, even with the mandible, over the sheet of leather, and tie it to the jaw; and command the patient to rest, and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the figure has changed, then let it rest for three days, and then reset what has changed; and apply plaster to it, with powder from the mill with plenty of egg white or flour from the husk, after you have removed the cerotomies; and put on another light layer of plaster, and if the plaster hardens, and the patient's condition does not change, let him be healthy for as long as he remains so; often it becomes healthy in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses form, then administer as we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and a wound together, then reward a small piece of the bone that is osteo; if subtle of the ostium are the instruments convenient to this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is tight, then enlarge it with fire according to your necessity.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have ostected all these pieces, and there is no delay, if the wound is wide, then put on it plasters convenient to this, to reduce the fever, as long as it is healthy.
de la forcele	of the lever
