Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	of the lever breaks many times before, over the shoulder, and the break is according to .ij. ways: or it is broken and dislocated in .ij., and there are pieces, and it is the easiest to restore; or there is a break with wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work if it is so that the break is without wound, you have  .ij. ministers, so that one holds the lever that is broken; and the others extend the neck towards the part; then make the break even on both sides, so that the form is as it should be, and there is no appearance or hair-splitting.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you have to extend more, so put a round staff of cloth or linen on the shoulder of the patient, and make it big according to your need; and lift and hold the lever, and draw the staff into your hand, so that you make the break even, as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the shoulder away from behind, so that it comes out perfectly, it is necessary that the patient lie down on his back and put his ear down; and the assistant raises the shoulder blade, until the bone of the shoulder is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then place the break on your sides, and if you find it broken, you should split it; and draw the pieces out lightly, and if the bone cannot be joined by any means, then take off the instrument with which you are treating; but keep the shoulder blade in place for surgery.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and it seems like a spoon, and is not hair, and should also be wide enough to accommodate the size of the bone and the ability of the work; and it has .ij. shoulders, if you can see, one wide and the other narrow, just as the fracture of the wound that you made when you split the bones.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are certain of the incision, if it is hot, and the fracture is small, or if you doubt about the incision, if you employ a drape or a tent, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if abscesses come, let it be wet with oil of rose, with almond, and wine; and put on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	For the extraction of bone, when there is pain and injury, it is that you put on the bone with plaster from the powder of the mill and with ash of egg, and put light stamps on, and put a spike under if you need one.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	then take a very long band of one palm wide, then put two layers of oilcloth on top, and plaster it on; then take a thin stick of two feet long, and wrap it around the bandage so that the head of the bandage is hanging down;
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and put the stake on the broken bone, and turn the bandage over your neck, and under the elbow, and around the arm; and take off one side at a time, and when you see that the bandage stays in place forward, and you clearly see that the stake does not move from above the bone, then take it all off every day, and when you feel that the joint is loose,
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort .i. petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a .xx. jors;	and make the patient lie on his back, and tie him when he sleeps . i . little ear pull out the shoulder, in order to raise the dislocation upwards; so will the break of the joint by the alignment of the shoulder be eased, where you bind the arm to the neck, and no bad accident comes, until .xx. days;
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en .xxviij. jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	then begin the cauterizing again, if you see that it is necessary, and hold and let it be like this until he is restored; and she is restored in 39 days, and less for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	from the break of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	For the break of the shoulder
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone is sticking out, and there is no pain when touched, then it is made to come up, and the bone, and do as we have said in the breaking of the shoulder to calm the abscess with heat.
de la brisure dou pis	of the breaking of the piece
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	If the piece is broken in half, it often comes apart, but when it does not, it causes great pain to the patient; and if it does not align properly, and sometimes it vomits blood, and the taste is bad in the broken bone, and the smell is terrible.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient lies down on his back, and you place a pillow under his head, then press his shoulders together, and join the ribs with hands, and carefully make it even in every way so that the figure of the bone is as it should be; then wrap it in a cloth, and fasten it to the bone, either with a string or something lighter, and tie it tightly, and adjust it hour by hour, and if it relaxes, you tighten it; and if it needs to be released, because of corrosion or itching that comes to the surface, or pain or abscess, then hasten to release it, and remove the covering, and treat it in a way appropriate to its condition; then remove the covering, and fasten it tightly until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	from a break in the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	I know that the rib fracture only comes from the outside, deep in the back, and does not bend much except because they are so thin; and it feels good at the examination to the two hands.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And if you restore it so that the break is even, as it should be; and then put on the plaster, and hold it with a splint, if you need one.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the rib fracture is facing inward, then the patient will feel great pain and aching, as if it were weeping; because the bone rubs against the membrane; and it becomes hoarse, and it vomits much blood, and this is a sign of bad health, and it has caused a great deal of trouble.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if it is from those who serve that it is necessary to administer meat that swells the belly, to drive the wind away towards the anus.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make this, unless hot poultices come, if it has not already come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, let the patient rest.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And no one says that we put poultices on the spot, to draw off the excess, and this is true; however, doubt exists that poultices can attract excesses to the site by weak disposition.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they said that one must cover the place of another's moistness with oil, and set tents between the ribs to make the space equal, then cure it from the plague cure, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain so that he cannot bear by the bone that stretches the tapestry, then there is doubt in the patient; therefore it is necessary to split over the place of the broken rib, and it is necessary to put there an instrument to ward off illness; and then it is necessary to trim the bone, and pull lightly, and then sew the two lips of the wound, if they are big, and cure them with poultices, until they are healed. And if abscesses come, then put on drapes wetted with oil, and place them; and while healing the place where it is necessary for an abscess to come, and let him rest on the rib or where he needs to, until they are healed.
de la brisure dou col	from the rib fracture
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	No one comes who breaks the bone of the neck, and that it falls; and also at the back of the spine.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent. Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	And when it is in anyone and you can see if he will be healed or not, if his hands are soft and swollen and dead and cannot move or stretch, and if you prick them with an needle, if they don't bleeds. Know that it is fatal in many dispositions, and if they don't bleed and feel good when they are extracted and there is no, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be healed, if he is put on treatment.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet. Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	And when similar things come to the spine of the back, and you can see if he will be healed or not, if his joints are soft and the accident is in his hands, and on his back wind comes out and excretes without will; and when it is put on its stomach, excretes without will. And when it is put on its back and it wants to stand, it cannot. Know that it is fatal: do not work in its treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come to him, then is the thing lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you put oil of rose or oil of musk on it if there is inflammation, until it is calm; then place it on a bandage and bind it, and tie it with a thread, and command to the patient to rest; and do not sleep in the part where he feels pain, until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is dislocated, if it needs to be covered with cloth; and bone the bone, then join together the two lips of the wound, if it is big, with a stitch, then treat it with ointment, bringing in charcoal, until it is healthy; and if the bone is broken, which is called "bone of the knee", if you hold your cup in your left hand, and place it equal to the other hand at your power, then put on the plaster and tie it up, if you need to; then hold it, and if any bones are dislocated, if it needs to be done, and bone it, and cure the wound until it is healthy.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the broken bone of the thigh
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	If the bone of the thigh is broken, and if it happens, let there be only a little bit of damage to the head; and smooth it out, and set it in place, declining it to the side, and coming to the patient's pain, and pointiness, and swelling where it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the setting in place if you extend your hand over it, as long as you are above the break; and know what the break is and what its shape is; and if the break is at the head, set the break equal to that which is natural.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if his break is long, or it declines inwardly, then let the patient lie on his belly until the mending of that break is arranged for him.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have made it even, then lay it on the plaster, and then put a board of wood or of timber upon it, and draw out the break so that it does not move; and employ the joint with bands at the sides, until the place is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on his side or back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess comes up, so long as it does not cause pain, until the abscess has been drained, and then return to the restoration, holding it in place as necessary, unless there is some other misfortune; and that is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	the dislocation of the shoulder
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And the 2 heads 2 ties, and lift them up, and cut the patient on 1 seat; then pour out some of the water on the broken arm to the elbow, and have a bucket of water ready; then put it on any heavy object or weight down; then put the break on equal hands together, until the break returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	The other way is that you lie the patient on his back, and hold his hand to his neck, then order 2 ministers that one holds what is on the break at your hands, and the others hold down all the ties, and extend each to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint .i. liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part. Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes .i. liien moien desoz l’assele, et .i. autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre .i. liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	Et s'il est nécessaire de faire une incision plus profonde, alors on attache avec un fil la rupture, et sur la rupture, et on place chacun des assistants à sa part. Et si la rupture est proche de la tête de l'épaule, il convient que tu places un fil de manière lâche derrière l'assise, et un autre vers le côté, derrière la rupture; et aussi, si la rupture est de ce côté-ci, il convient de placer un fil légèrement, sans effort, tant que la rupture reste droite sur son emplacement, et sur sa direction; puis placez la rupture comme elle convient, et serrez-la, si les apoptes ne viennent pas.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if apoplexy comes, then do not tie it up before 21 days, and put on the wound oil mixed with rosin, until the apoplexy is calm; then tie it up, and the way to tie it up is that you place the plaster on the rupture, and then you join the arm to the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the side; and wrap a cloth around it, and tie it up on the arm, so that the arm is in its natural position, unless something hinders it, or the bone does not break.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, then use a splint, and put on the rupture a splint wider and stronger than the others, and leave between each splint 2 inches of space, and let each splint be as large as to pass through the rupture 3 inches from each side; then tie up on the splints, so as I said at the beginning of the chapter on the plaster on the rupture, more strongly and less by moving away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns .iij. jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	And if you see the seat of the stars and the extraction, as we said, in the hour that you restore the broken member, and you doubt the incision warm, let it bind until the seventh day, as we said; then look at each one .iiij. days to see, so that itching does not flourish or come into place, or that the return of sensation cannot come to the member because it is too much restricted. If it is done, as we said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse. Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.	And if no such accident comes, if it is not removed after three days or more, and the patient sleeps on his back, and has his hands on his stomach; then place a clean piece of lamb's skin evenly over the broken member, and look every hour during the day or night that the figure of the broken member does not move, or that the ligaments are not relaxed; if it is healing by the power of medicine, and give him meat as we have said, in such a way that the food is at the first subtle level; and when he begins to improve, let it be thick. It is customary that the shoulder and leg should be put back in 40 days; and then it must be removed and bath and medicines of ointments applied to promote healing. And if the rigidity is ugly and sticky, do not remove it after one day or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of the break in the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of 2 bones, which are called the "fosciles," one small and one large; the small one lies in front of the large one, and the two together make up the arm. The large foscile can break off by itself, or the small one, or perhaps both at once.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When the small foscile is broken, the healing is easy, and when the large one is broken, it is a bad healing, and more painful than when both are broken at once. If it is only the small foscile that is broken, then the appropriate thing is to extend it lightly, and make it even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it is the large foscile that needs to be stretched more strongly; and extend it on .i. side, and turn the pouchet of the hand up higher than the other sides, and the small fingers lower than the others, so that the patient does not suffer any pain; then stretch the ministers' arms to the dislocated part at their hand, or at a .i. line, and another minister's arm above it. And then make the patient lie even, according to his best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the break is into pieces, then put each one in its place, and if there is any that does not grasp the handle, and you cannot restore it to its place, then mend it with nails and wood, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the cutter to the wound, I have spoken of it to the singular chapître; so take the cure.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir vj. esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en .ij.; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And if in the beginning of the restoration comes abscesses, so glue .i. a drape of cerote made of oil and white wax, that is not too hard or too soft; and put the drape above subtilely, as long as the abscess is calmed down. And then oil the cerote, and put the plaster of the powder of the mill with much tar, because put the splints, and be that the splint of the briseure is more farther, and a little wider than others; and know that it must have vj. splints or arms in many dispositions: whether the briseure is in one bone, or in .ij.; and stretch up above the briseure rather than other part, and all days less to be removed, if I said at the beginning of the chapître; and be the drape that are on the briseure soft and moist, and not too hard or too rough; and be the thread, of which it is stretched, of linen, not too thick nor too fine, as we have said. And reward the member and the joint after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And if some bad accidents come to the member, as pruritus that comes to the member, so that you must rinse the member with hot water, until the pruritus is calmed down; and let the member rest no longer confined. And then begin again the stretching, and if the ligaments are soft and the bones desevrez, and similar things, if you address it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if take ward that the stretching not come to the member, por ceu that it is too confined, so that you must make it soft  .i. bit, and leave it thus for some days, as long as the stretching runs, and then stretch it again.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And if any of these things that we have said do not come to the patient, so it is not a dislocation until .xx. days, or so long as he can feel, then let him put his hands on his neck, and make his neck even, and keep away from movement and change, and sleep on his back; and know that this broken piece has been healed in .xxx. days or in .xxxv., and perhaps in .xx. days, according to the compositions and complexions of virtues.
de la brisure de la main	Of the break in the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that at the back of the hand and on both sides there are few breaks, and it comes but a little often.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the plant of the hand is broken or plied, so it is that the patient dies, and if he sees straight before him even; then let him put his hand on the table extended, and extend the members of the bones that are broken, and make them even, until they are well joined together; and put the plaster and staples, unless there are any, then put a steele according to the quantity of the place; and be wrapped up in 1. drapes of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if it breaks within the paregoric around the navel of the plant, then make a rope of drapels, and instruct the patient that he estrengs to his navel; and then he pulls out with a long drapeil, and is the size of a great rope from a sheaf, and draws him, if it comes.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if it breaks at the end, then you should put a stake on it, and another one in the plant, so that the hands are open and straight; then tie it tightly around the hand, and seal the bond between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if it breaks at one of the two, then you should put it in a straight position, as it comes; and tie it with the plant, and if you see that there is one that needs to be lifted, do not move; and if it breaks on the other two, then put it in a straight position, and bind it to the healthy one after it; or all four together, holding them tightly, so that they can move, or you should put it on a stake, as I said; and take care of the restoration and arrangement of the aposteme, and help those who come, as I said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken shoulder
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bones of the hip are often broken, and one can see very well when they turn forward and backward; and the cure is this: first, you ligate above the fracture, and second, you do so below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	The patient lies on his face, then extends each minister, or servant, of the body equally to his side; and that is when the fracture is mended.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure. Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	If the fracture is near the root of the hip, then one minister should be placed above the knuckle, and another below the fracture; and if it is near the knee, then one minister extends the leg upward, and another downward; then he makes the bone equal with his two hands, as nature has made it, and then he applies the plaster, and ligates it, so that the wound does not open.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	If there is an abscess, then he should let it rest and return to his work and treatment; the time for the operation is determined in this way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap around the fracture .i. bend hard double in .ij. or .iij., and wait for the superfluity, then turn the leg until the heels come to the root of birth, and stick i.e. a long thread between the buttocks and the leg, delving the knee cap off, and bring the head of the thread above; then turn on the leg and the buttocks the bend, then put the stork-beak on the fracture, and put a stork-beak on the bone of the leg; then employ the space left between the leg and the buttocks with drapels of cloth to make the compression equal, then begin to bind it form iij. twists or iiij. on the fracture; and as you go up on the fracture, and less the compression; then take the 2j. threads that you have stuck between the leg and the buttocks, and tie iij. stork-beaks that are above, then return to the knee cap until you come off of it; and the compression, so that it does not move from its place, then leave it like this, then if it comes not a pimple or swelling or another appearance.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it should happen, if it loosens, and addresses the one who has come, if as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that grip, if it is necessary to move them, if you can; and if you cannot, if it is necessary to split the place, and pull forcefully; and heal it as we have said, until it is healthy.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never is the buttocks broken here because we put stork-beaks, if as in the shoulder and arm; however, when restoring it in this way, do not clatter the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the cure is completed in .1. days, or less or more, according to the variations of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	from the knee joint
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	For in the joint of the knee there is sometimes a little fracture, but it often heals over and over again. And if it does fracture, it may be only a crack or a hole, and if it is broken, it does not hurt as much as if it were a wound.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that if what is broken is equal to what is left at its ends, as long as it can be put together again, then set the plaster and put a round stake there, if you need one, and fasten it as we have said for other fractures, whether it is an apostume or something else; also set each accident in such a way that it becomes healthy.
de la brisure de la jambe	the break of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	that in the leg are .ij. bones, so that one is called by right "mustelz", and the others are called "foscile"; and it is the same break as that of the arm, and for this reason the restoration is the same as that of the arm equally, and the operations are all the same.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if the two bones are broken together, then the leg turns on all sides.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the fine bones are broken, then it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain and one can see it well; and then return to the dislocation. Then apply extension, and make it even, and bind the stars evenly; but nevertheless, it is fitting that the fracture should be ugly, and there are more pieces, so that the extension should be smaller and lighter; and align according to your virtue.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have finished all your work, so take .ij. twists of twisted rope that purple the leg on one side and the other, and are long of the leg from the knee to the ankle; then wrap them in .ij. pieces of cloth above and below, and tie this ligature at mid-leg, and in this ligature the leg cannot descend to the right or to the left, and so it is good; and no one administer .i. twists of long rope, and if it is twisted, and put on the leg to ward off movement, and properly make one out of the fracture or there is a sore; and stir each day the leg, to see if there is an abscess or some other accident; if the cure as long as it is healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the bone fracture of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no fracture of the bone, but the bone of the foot comes in one fracture and two times broken, and it has never been except that it was shattered in several dispositions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if it should happen that the bones of the foot are broken, and you see these bones surmounting one another, put this patient down on the ground like he wants to walk, and then now place your foot upon his, where those bones have risen up, then press them back down into their places; then apply the plaster and set it in place, and under the foot's belly a small flat tablet of 2.5 ounces; then bind it around the foot in front, then since you have wrapped these drapes, and other things that you need to do.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	When three or four days have passed, if the swelling has gone down, for you will find the bones even, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there is any of the two broken, if you reset it, if, as we said, to the two of them in length; and let one be a little wider, then place under the foot that small tablet I spoke of, and set it in place; and if there are 1.5 or 2., or more, broken, if you place on each of them an eagle according to their quantity, wrapped in 1. drape of linen, and set the tablet under the foot; and let it be under the belly of the foot, so that it is well covered.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it is necessary that you do not forget the other things that I said about other injuries, as soon as we have said them; and help each accident as it is necessary.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the breaking of the bone in the upper arm
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone is broken in the upper arm, if the woman is seated, then she should be tilted towards the back and supported from behind; then the doctor should fill the cavity of the nature with cotton, and put in also a large piece of cloth; then the woman should stand up, and bend her arm little by little, and then take out the cotton, until it comes to the opening of the nature, and the bone returns with the cloth; and when she urinates, if she takes out the cotton, and when she has urinated, replace it, and in this way do for six days or more: so the fracture will be healed, and the pain will go away. Take a bladder from a lamb, and tie a cord around it, and pour all of the bladder into the nature; then blow into the bladder, forming a shape until the bladder is empty: the nature will then return the fracture; then fill it with cotton, and leave it like that for some days, until it has healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	And when the bone in the hand of the man or woman is broken, if it is restored as we have said before concerning the bone in the hip; and these breaks are not hidden from him who devotes himself to study and practice, and reads my book. For the break signifies many things to the right way of restoration: let us therefore understand them.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the vagina, when it is broken, take a neck of an goose and pour it into the vagina; then wrap fabrics around it, and leave it like that for .ii. days or more, and it will be healed in hospital.
de brisure avec plaie	about a break with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is appropriate for one who has a break with a wound, even if it is great, such as the bone of the jaw or shoulder or similar, to be healed now, so that the healed ones that we have mentioned testify.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, except for the vitriol stain, then you have nothing else, then start restoring the break in this very hour, or the same day, unless the pustules come out.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if the pustules come out, then delay restoring it for a new day, as long as the pustules are calm, and do not touch them either on the third day or on the fourth, because you would bring about a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if his nose is broken, it appears at the tip of the nose that has been revealed; then you should put your hands lightly on the extension of the tip.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extensions are not equal to your hands in length, then take this instrument made of iron, which is 2.5 inches long and 1/4 inch wide; and according to the quantity of the wound, use as much as is necessary for each cure of a broken nose; and let it be round and a little thick, so that it does not press on the member at your opening, and be sharp in front and thick in the middle, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre. Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And it is called "palainche," because the broken end of the bone should be placed on the tip of the nose; and it should be struck once, until it sets, and they should be even with each other. And if the break is small, then this instrument cannot take the bone well, so you should chip off the tip of the nose, until the instrument can grasp the bone.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring the bone back, as we have said, if you chip off a piece of a suitable instrument, or an incisor or file, at your command; then take that which remains in the bone and of small cuts.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil. Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And when the jaw is brought back, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place. If it is in its place, then wet it with wine-based black dye, and properly so if it is seared; and do not put on the wound wax or anything else that has oil, lest it bring about infection and corruption; then administer stones when you have restored the jaw, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover everything around it according to the quantity of the wound, and take good care that the wound should not be strained with the break; and many times this has been done to the sick, and they have come to die or corrode at all times; and let the extractions be softer and more gentle than those of other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie. Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that a bad accident has not come to it, as we have said, and you feel pain at the place, then it is not appropriate to put on stones; but wrap it in a tough fabric instead of stones, and bind it. And when you see after one day or two days break out at the wound, then remove that which you have put on with wine, and put on the ointment that heals wounds, as we said, with tetrafarmaçon and similar things.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is appropriate to loosen the member three times a day, in the morning and at dusk, until it is healed and whole.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the members are arranged in such a way that the bow moves down lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if someone bumps into it, and he cannot hold it but it comes together again with a click, because there are small pieces of bone, so you must pull the wound apart, and remove all these painful pieces that cause the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant. Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if a fistula appears at the site of corruption, or in any other way, so it is necessary that you treat it according to what he says in his chapter above. And when the bone is broken and opens up on the limb, as with the bones of the hip or shoulder, and similar large limbs, do not pull it out, for many die if you do; but leave it until it putsrefies; then treat the wound, if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of bruses that come from the soil
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We come many times after the health of the broken bone, most often when it is near the joint, and the ugly thing to see is the shape of the member; and by chance cannot do the work of its natural limbs.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care, then, if we find him ill: if he is administered stinging medicines, such as aloes, incense, myrrh, and sarcacollege, ochre, and similar ones; so that you do not apply any of these things, or all together, and mix them with wine of the stinging sort, or with a lot of honey, or with oil; and put them on the swelling in layers, and bind it well, and do not remove the bandage for many days; and then take it off, and start again, until the swelling is gone; or you hold it to one piece of felt well made; because the property of felt is that it takes away all swelling from the limbs; and if the swelling has turned hard like stone, then it must be cut open, so that the excess appears; or you have it cut by a barber, as long as it is hard, and cure it as long as it is well.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the member which is weak after the ward
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the bone is set and remains weak and thin after ward: either because it was too tightly bound, and was not bound as it should have been; or because there were too many ties, and he could not come to the member's aid; or because of too much swelling; or because of too great movements, not in its time; or because he has little blood in his body, so he is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat and make the body lean, until the bones multiply in him; and give him a bath, and give him joy and comfort; then put wax on the member so that the wax attracts his great thirst, and rinse it often with fresh water, until the thirst goes to the member; and return to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	the wounded member after health
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the member is twisted after restoration, and the bone is broken, and the form of the member is ugly, nonetheless it does not lose its natural function: do not believe the foolish people who say that you must break the member all over again, and many such fools have done this in our land; and these practices are blamed, and great harm happens to them, and sometimes they even die. However, if the nodules and torments are fresh, it is good that they be bathed in hot water, or herbs with soothing properties be boiled, such as billets of turtle, and roots, and melilot, and similar things; and the poultice should be made with a soothing ointment, such as a well-made daquilon, and you take the muskeg of turtle, and confit it with linseed oil or ghee oil, and make a poultice with it; or you take ripe figs, and grind them with hay of colts, and similar medicines that soften the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes. Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And no bone should be knotted so as to be rubbed continually and for a long time with damp hands. And the member should be moved every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the joints are twisted and hardened, as in the case of stone, it is necessary to open them with iron, covering the bone up to the joint, cutting lightly with a sharp knife; and put poultice and study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	This is the beginning of the book on dislocations:
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, resulting in misaligned limbs, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs at any joint, if it is now necessary to bring back into alignment by force.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le déplace a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if it is late, and the swells increase, and by chance we put it back in its place; for this is not good that we move it when it is swollen: many times it brings spam and other pains; however, when it comes, if one heals the patient, then let him rest, as long as the abscess is calmed down; then raise the member with hot water and oil, then gently adjust it, and cure each member as the healing comes.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the treatments of dislocations of the shoulder joint up to the tips of the fingers.
des mandibules	of the mandible.
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Here is the translation of the text:
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocations are little, so return by them several dispositions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is entirely and completely done, then you must reset it quickly in the hospital, and do not delay.
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de .ij. pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	and in this way that the ministers wet the head of the patient with a little pot of medicine on one of his hands at the root of the dislocation of the mandible inside the mouth, so the dislocations are of .ij. parts; and the other two hands should be apart, to make it even; and instruct the patient that he makes his jaws soft, and moves them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And he looks at the metal to make it even, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if they are grimy, certainly the two jaws are together, but if they are rammed with hot water and oil, so that they are gently brought back; do not wait to bring them back, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are brought back evenly, and the mouth of the sick person is well closed with a mollifying substance, if you put it on drapes soaked in oil and wax, then gently move them away from each other;
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre .ij. cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	and the sick person sleeps on his back, and his jaws are between two pillows, so that he does not move them from side to side or strain them, but eats soft food, until the pains have gone away, and the jaws are no longer painful.
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then cut what he wants lightly, and do not work to open the mouth to eat and drink, until the jaw is well tied and healthy.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be reset to their places in an hour, and they do not return to their places, then fever and usual colds come, and perhaps stomach upset, and perhaps vomiting of clear liquid.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see that it is death; and many times he dies who has it, in nineteen days.
de la forcelle	forcelle
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceps cannot dislocate from the cost over the course of its extension and from the foot, and is dislocated only once to the outside, and one can feel it well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	And the restoration is that the patient lies down on his back, and extends his arms; and then press the joint with your palm, and it will come back; then put on the plaster and the bandage, and tie it up;
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	and the head that is beside the cost cannot be dislocated; unless it is, and if it is dislocated once, let him return to his place, as we have said; then put on the plaster and the bandage, and tie it up, and instruct the patient to rest until he is well.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	and also here is how to bring back the shoulder that is dislocated from its place when it has been dislocated.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc .iij. manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	is dislocated except for two ways: either it is dislocated from the part of the shoulder to the arm; and the second is dislocated from the foot of the bone; and by chance it is dislocated from the top, and this happens little.
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	and do not dislocate behind the shoulder, and do not dislocate inside for the neck; and many times dislocates out towards the arm, but nevertheless to those who have little money, because at these it is usually admitted to hospital; and to those who have enough money, let it go back in pain, and return in pain.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	and by chance some men have percussion or cracking, and breaks the shoulder with a hot apoplexy, and thinks that it is dislocated by this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is therefore necessary for you to test it, as far as you are certain of it; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And is distinguished from the dislocation when it goes down towards the shoulder, and distinguishes between the sick and the healthy shoulder, and you will find between them a great difference.
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and you will find at the head of the shoulder a depression, and put the shoulder back on the neck at the head of the shoulder, just as if it were an egg; and the patient cannot bring his hand to his nose, nor move it at all.
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	and also, if it is dislocated upwards, unless it is hidden, for you will find it clearly at the neck.
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	and this way of dislocation is not used when it is new, or when the patient has become ill.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the way is that the minister holds the patient's hand up, then puts the splint out of the socket, and raises the joint by force to its place; and the minister holds the hand up, and extends it up again, then puts it out; and there comes sudden pain.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	And if it does not come as we have said with the hands after a few days, so that the patient is bathed in warm water; and mild and soothing remedies are applied, such as an infusion of alfalfa and fenugrec and mimosa in water, and it is applied;
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	then put a soft cloth on the patient's back, and put a hard but not too hard or too soft piece of wood under it, then put the minister's hand on the shoulder with care, and draw it up;
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	and others ministers taint the head of the disease, so that it does not move downward; this shoulder returns all at once, and you see if they are reset according to this way:
et est que tu faices estre present .i. home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and so you make be present .i. a man who is greater than the patient; and let it stand on the side of the body, and pull up the shoulder of the patient, and raise the shoulder in front of the patient, so that the patient hangs down.
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre. Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	and other ministers pull the hand of the disease downward toward the stomach. And if the patient is too light, then weight him down with something heavy, and the dislocation will return now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche .i. lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com .i. pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	And the head is reset in another way: and it is set as a.i. nail, and is not too big nor too small; and
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	Then, treat the patient, but let there be a drape of salt water over him, and let the patient remain lying down longwise; then stretch out his hand on one side, so that the joint returns to its place securely.
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren .i. tison de .ij. bras de grant et .iiij. dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not return because of all these things that we have said, then do this cure: take a piece of wood from the arm of a strong and tall tree, which has a hole through it in the middle, so that the head can pass perfectly into dislocation according to this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then put it over the top of the head with salt water, so that it does not burn the patient, and then place it into dislocation on the patient's shoulder; and extend your arms along the wood, and place the aid on the wood, and the arm at the head of the hand, and then place the arm on a small board of a certain size, and let the body hang from one side: the joint will now return.
