Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, in whatever way, you must then put down on the shoulder a piece of wool that is even, and then put on the pomander of the mill, with incense and ash of ash, all over the shoulder and around, then pull it out of dislocation gradually, and tie the ligature on the pomander, and embrace the hand to the neck, and let the hands remain in this way.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he should drink little, so long as the members are comfortable, for they will heal more quickly; and then drink more after a day or two, and move them. And if they are stiff and not softened, they are healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a iij. pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint has moved from its place due to moisture which has come, or due to another cause, it is necessary that you treat it with cauterization three times, as we have described above, with the paste of cauterization.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and after five or six days the joint does not hold and cannot raise its arm upright, then you know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder has been cut or stretched or softened; and you know that the joint has never been set in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is above the loins, and the breastbone, or behind, is made by an impact, and by stretching of the arms, and I move it another way; and treat it until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing comes stiffness in the member, and late movement, so the patient bathes many times, until that stiffness is relaxed, and returns to its first nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the joint
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Sache that the jointure of the shoulder is dislocated forward and backwards, and perhaps less so on the sides, and if it is dislocated in all directions, one can see and feel it clearly; and let it be dislocated according to its shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement. Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	And when you join the dislocated shoulder with the sound one, if you can see it clearly. For the joint is dislocated and cannot bend the arm or touch its shoulder.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you bring it back in the same way as the chest is opened, for if the chest were opened, there would be great grief in doing so; and by chance it cannot be brought back from all and everywhere, especially from behind; it is worse than other dislocations, and causes great pain, and by chance it leads to death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is, when it is such that you can bring it back, that you extend its hand to your 1 . 2 hands; and its arms are spread out, and the hands between the base of the thumb and the knuckle, up and down, and press the joint together with its palm roots, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, then come back when he doubles his hand to his other hand, and pull on the side that is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	And if it does not return to its place, then give a strong extension; and it is that the two extend the arm, and pull it down the two, so that it does not move at the extension; then turn the arms of each side, then that you have wrapped a double long and wide cloth;
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	and when he sees the joints of his hand, if he does not apply any oil to soften the joints, then tighten them together until they recover.
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	and when it is in place, if he puts on plaster with ash and honey, and tightens it, and holds the arm up to the neck of the sick person, and leaves it for a few days, then loosens it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, then loosen the bandage and leave it; and if you see that the joint does not move well, then begin again with plaster and the bandage, and leave it for a while until it is firmly placed, then loosen it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse .i. jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	And if he feels pain after resetting the joint, and it is painful, then bathe and rub it well, and press until it is soothed; or you put on the joint a layer of sheep's fat, then leave it for one day and one night, then loosen it, and let him enter or bathe.
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai .ij. fois ou .iij., tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	and when it rains, he gently rubs the joint and then puts the child back on his feet and into the bath; and so he does .ij. or 1.iij. times, until he is healthy; and if you see it, put it on the end of a wet towel that has been heated with butter, and draw it up; and it will come back to its position.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	the dislocated hand comes back more easily than other joints; however, it is necessary to return it to its place immediately after dislocation, when the joint is swollen, or else an abscess will form.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And if you put the diseased hand on a table, and extend its fingers, and look at it, so that he puts his palm against the joint, and presses it until it returns;
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	All the same, you must make sure that he is lying in a good position; then place the patient's back of his hand on a table for extension and for bringing it back.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele aparance de la jointure. S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, then place the patient's back of his hand on a table, and look at the appearance of the joint; if it comes back now, that is good.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, then cut off the appendages with sharp knives and let them bleed; then he leaves it like this without a surgeon's aid.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot set it in place after several days, then wait for the joint to heal.
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	and should not be told to the patient that as long as his hands are wet, he can't extract anything: so you know that the nerves are cut, or the artery; if there is no other device but to extract by delicate cautery the case, and perhaps nothing else.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when his hands are in place, let them rest on the plaster that we have said, then extract and leave it for a day or two, then remove it and leave it like that.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he can't move it well, and there is no fracture, if the water is warm, and rub it until it is well.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the two hands
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	None of the time are the joints of the hand dislocated at each side, none of the time to the back of the palm or the belly;
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	Then are the joints, and press the dislocation to your knuckles until it comes back, then support the head of the two joints, and move it towards the part where it is joined;
et le laisse .ij. jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit,	and then leave it.ij. days, and then set it straight that day; and if it is stiff, as we have said, and dislocates that day, and makes it move, and sets it back in place; and do this often, until it is loose, and
et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	and also do this if it is dislocated at the base of the hand, and do so as you have done before, until it is well; and also do this when it is dislocated from the other side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Dou desaluement de l'eschinee dou dos.
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	For the dislocation of the shoulder or collarbone, if there is one or more dislocations, without treatment, for fear that the patient will die quickly.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les .ij. cuixes ou li dui bras ou .j.	And the signs are that the excretions come out without will, cannot hold them, and often the limbs are weakened, or the two thighs or two arms or one.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a iiij. pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	And often the eschyne is mute in three parts: that which is mute at the back is called "gilbositez".
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	If it is due to a deformity brought on by childhood, then there is no cure or recovery from all of this.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And those that come from falls or blows or similar things, the ancient ways of treating them with great words did not bring much benefit to all of this.
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	But I have simplified it according to my intention, and have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in the deformity that comes before, there is no cure or healing.
et ausi cele que vient droitement en .ij. costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	and so too those who come from the back, if I say, for they cannot be cured except properly.
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en .i. leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	and so too that the patient lie face up on an even surface, and have a harness put on them, so that they do not bleed.
puis fiche .i. tison au chief en terre forment, et .i. autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et .i. autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	and then set a log on the ground under the patient's head, and another between his feet, and tie a rope around the patient's chest, and another between his knees, and another between his ankles;
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les .ij. tisons;	and the two ministers know the ropes, one at the head and the other between the feet, among the two logs;
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	and are firmly closed, the twine so as we said, and the mirror sets its palms on the spine, until he comes round.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de .iij. bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if she does not come back by this cure, take a table of 12 inches long, and shave off the wall, and let the patient be on one side, and pour the top of the table off the wall, then put the middle of the table on the spine;
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	and put the mirror's tips on the other top of the table, and press well, until he comes back to place; and if you see this, do it with your other hand.
Et est que tu fiches .ij. tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez .ij. autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And it is that you stick 12 torches on the top of the sick person with a big arm, and put them between each torch, up and down, a palm's length apart;
et ait en chescun tison .i. pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns .ij. tisons ait .i. tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en .ij. tornans .ij. petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	and place each splinter .i. on the edge, or let it run, and are the splinters firmly in the ground so that they do not move, and between each .ij. splinters is one splinter turning, because the string turns, and have in the .ij. turners .ij. small splinters of a palm long, to turn the string;
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	and then tie the string that is between the splinters to the top of the hook, and the other string toward the stones at the other hook, and each of the ministers turns his string on all the string, and the master puts the needle even as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de .iij. dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it is even, put on dried ochre with a lot of oil, and then the plasters, and then the board of a tablet of 1.iij. inches long, that purple the head of the gibbus and the part of the spine healthy, then tie it with a string as we have said, and use subtle oil to the patient until he is well;
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc,	and if no thing comes to the end of health, so administer soft and soothing medicines with the tablet that we have said above; and never administer one tablet,
et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	and never comes the appearance in the posterior spondyle of the back, and thought it is dislocations; and this is the bone that opens, so that one must not have presumption: by chance would come death.
des dislocations de la hainche	of the hip joint dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	tell that the hip and shoulder joints only come as dislocations, not otherwise; and the hip joint is dislocated according to three.iiij. parts: within and outside, and in front and behind; and most inside, and least in front and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the knowledge of its dislocations within is that when one joins the ill leg with the healthy, it is more distant, and opens more of the ill foot than of the healthy one, and cannot double its ill knee on fire;
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	and is the place where the thigh comes from an abscess hot, for this reason the head of the leg comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of that person who has it, if this accident is opposite to these before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of that person who has it, if this leg is well in accordance with the condition; nevertheless, do not double the knee, and if you make him walk, he cannot go before, and he holds his urine back, and swells the ankle, and when he walks, he goes on the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of that person who has it behind, if he cannot spread his knee and double, and this leg is more twisted than the other, and the joint of the hip is in place at the side of the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The ramening of this dislocation is that if you reset it and the dislocation is old, and it lingers according to its disposition, there is no cure for it; and it only comes about that he has assumed himself.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in this one where the dislocation is fresh, and it's of the iii manneres of dislocations, if you hasten to reset the joint, and make it come back together and go away again and turn it to the right and left; perhaps so will it return, and there is no need for any other cure.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles .i. ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a .ij. mains, ou a .i. liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not return in this way, then you must get a very strong minister, and hold the leg very firmly with .ij hands, or with a .i. strap tied to the loins;
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	and with others ministers he extends his hand over the joint in such a way that he can hit his hands together, then he ties a strap to the loins; and another minister ties the hair of the strap;
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	and are extended upwards and downwards together at once, as long as the patient is raised from the ground once, and remains still.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common to three appearances, and when the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance. Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	If that is not the case, then you must put a cure on his back. When the dislocations are in the parison, if you put a curcuma pouder on the patient's back, and hold it there for an hour, and then let it fall by its own weight, and spread it with a cloth;
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	then apply to his arms, and embrace the great line of the troublesome cuije, and extend it in this way: now it will return to its place; and this manner of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les .ij. piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les .ij. talons, et sus les .ij. genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue .ij. dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot hold it in this way that we have said, then you must tie the .ij. feet of the sick together with a strong cord above the .ij. heels, and above the .ij. knees, so that the sick leg is extended more than the other two.
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre .ij. bras de lonc; puis comande a .j. ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	Then hang him by the neck from a beam, and let him be 2 feet above the ground; then order 1 minister to embrace the sick person's waist, and let other ministers hang with the sick person, who embraces the waist tightly, for the joints now come back quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne .i. liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation is at a distance, let the sick person lie down as we have said in that which concerns the gimbose, and tie the 1 cord properly on the sick leg, and also on the foot.
puis met .ij. tisons, .i. au chief et .i. autre as piez, puis fiche .i. tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	Then put 2 torches, 1 at the head and 1 between the legs, then place 1 torch between the sick person's thighs.
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	and put up damp flags behind, so that the patient does not bleed, then extend each minister toward him, and let him place the dislocation equal to his hand.
S’elle revient, c’est boin. Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If it returns, that is good. If not, put it on .ie. a table, and press it as we have said in the gibosity, and lay the patient down on the side coast.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, extend the injured leg far away, and according to what I have said; and place his hand so that it is on top of the injured hip, then press with the other hand, and turn it downward toward the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les .ij. hainches;	And when the dislocation is in the back, so it is not possible to extend the injured leg far away, and it does not stand on its own, but rather it must be placed as if the person were lying down with his back to the ground, as we have said in the laying-out of the legs;
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	and let it hang down on his face, and the bone extended as we have said above, and must hold firm pressure on the joint to the table;
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	and will be able to stretch his legs out, and they will be even; then remove the poultices, put on the plaster, and draw out with a bandage, so that the ankle does not move;
et se repose .iij. jors ou .iiij., puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse. iij. jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	and rest for 3-4 days, then remove the poultices, and put on the plaster; and if you see that they are even, draw them out, as before, and let it be. 3-4 days; then remove the poultices, and have him walk around loudly, until the limbs feel comfortable again.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of a dislocated kne
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The genous are dislocated according to .iij. ways: that is to say, inside and outside, and behind; and do not dislocate in front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the signs are these: instruct the patient that he should bend his knee to his chest, and if it does not go to his chest, know that it is dislocated.
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	and the setting right of all these is that you should make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and place your back on his face, and put his foot on your knees;
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les .ij. costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	then take his knee between your palms, and pull it back between your two, then bend the .iij. knees together as if you were sitting; and other ministers extend his foot, until the genous returns to its place, and the signs are that he has bent his knee lightly to his chest.
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort .iij. jors ou iiij., puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	and bind the plaster on top, and make the leg rest in the crotch, and join them together firmly. .iiij. days or iiij., then take it off; and do not work the patient to walk, until the members are comfortable again.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the members are not in place, then administer strong stretching, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until they are healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel bone
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	the heel bone is never dislocated, and it never dislocates completely, inside out and upside down.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And these are the signs that the ankle is dislocated, and test before the part where it is dislocated.
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	they are brought back if they are light, and must be extended slightly with their hands when they are completely dislocated.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne .i. ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	and when it is dislocated from the top, if it is convenient that you make sit the patient upright, and tie him down.
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre .ij. fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	then train the foot to you at your right hand, and then to the left at your left hand.
et fai ce .ij. fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	and do this .ij. times, as we said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it comes back, it is good; if not, the work begins again, because it comes back;
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche .i. passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	if it can't come back like this, take the patient by the back on the ground, and put 1 pass firmly in the ground between his hips, and wrap a cloth around it so that it doesn't hurt the patient;
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a .i. liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	then put a minister's hip, and another minister extends the foot with his hands or with a .ij. chain that he ties around it, so that it lies on the collar of the foot;
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	then extend each minister equally, and let the 1 pass be close between the hips of the patient to hold the patient when you stretch him out;
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	and then make the dislocated joint equal with your hands, and other ministers will tan the healthy leg at the heel, and the dislocation will return completely.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it is done, if you apply the plaster and press it down, and the extract is formed, and tie the foot to the leg, and guard against the cords that are on the heel behind being too tight;
puis le laisse .ij. jors ou .iij., et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par .iiij. jors;	then leave it on for .ij. days or .iij., and if the extract is formed, then remove it after the third day, and do not let the patient go out, because he will be ill for .iiij. days;
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	and if he goes before that term is up, it is not yet secure that he has not dislocated again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses form, so it is necessary that you calm them down, as we have said elsewhere, until they are healthy.
des dois	of the two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two are dislocated, if it is kindly extended without work, and that is a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus .i. leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocations are in no pain of the feet of the feet, if it is necessary that you make sit the patient on a plain or a table all straight, and place your foot on what opens from these joints, then press with your foot forming, until he comes back;
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a .ij. chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse .iij. jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when it is even, and there is nothing open, then set the foot down on a table at .iij. shoulders, then extract it shaped, and leave it for .iij. days, then let it lie; and let it rest, as long as it is well.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When the wound comes with the dislocation, and one seeks to restore it, many times the patient has died:
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	if you are not presumptuous in the cure, and you have not used it for a long time, and if you are pitiless and merciful and slow, and not bold:
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	and apply at the beginning of things soothing paste to the abscess, and leave the patient in the hand of God, if you don't see any hope for health.
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	and when you see hope, then immediately set the member back in place so that the abscesses may heal;
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	and when the member is back in place, then apply soothing paste to the abscess and treat the wound, if necessary, with dry ointment;
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	and if there is a fracture and broken bones, and do as we have said in simple illnesses;
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors. Amen	and guard yourself from entering the path of fear, according to what I have said, because this will cause you great harm according to your Creator, and for the sake of preserving your body and soul. Amen
Explicit le romen de fisique	Here is the translation of the text:
